<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b0d35a27-046e-4fe9-bef4-a9d28f6b8465'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText7627915160406644048" style="display:none">Fairy tales are just the beginning.<br /><br />The Masked Man is on the loose in the Land of Stories, and it's up to Alex and Conner Bailey to stop him...except Alex has been thrown off the Fairy Council, and no one will believe they're in danger.<br /><br />With only the help of the ragtag group of Goldilocks, Jack, Red Riding Hood, and Mother Goose and her gander, Lester, the Bailey twins discover the Masked Man's secret scheme: He possesses a powerful magic potion that turns every book it touches into a portal, and he is recruiting an army of literature's greatest villains!<br /><br />So begins a race through the magical Land of Oz, the fantastical world of Neverland, the madness of Wonderland, and beyond. Can Alex and Conner catch up to the Masked Man, or will they be one step behind until it's too late?<br /><br />Fairy tales and classic stories collide in the fourth adventure in the bestselling Land of Stories series as the twins travel beyond the kingdoms!</span>

Can Alex and Conner catch up to the Masked Man, or will they be one step behind until it's too late?<br /><br />Fairy tales and classic stories collide in the fourth adventure in the bestselling Land of Stories series as the twins travel beyond the kingdoms! <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_810727235" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/810727235" />
    <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner"><img alt="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588471351p2/7366569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/810727235?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner">Fafa&#39;s Book Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316406895" href="/book/show/23657459-beyond-the-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer810727235&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer810727235" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14685245277339412210">This book was absolutely wonderful! As usual it was written beautifully and had an amazing plot to boast. <br/><br/>The book starts off with the late Fairy-godmother meeting with Hans Christian Anderson. Through their interaction the audience finds out that The Masked Man is in fact her other son Lloyd. They are not twins but instead a few years apart (it's not specified how many). The brothers happen to look exactly like their father so that's why Alex thought it was her father. Through this interaction </span>
  <span id="freeText14685245277339412210" style="display:none">This book was absolutely wonderful! As usual it was written beautifully and had an amazing plot to boast. <br /><br />The book starts off with the late Fairy-godmother meeting with Hans Christian Anderson. Through their interaction the audience finds out that The Masked Man is in fact her other son Lloyd. They are not twins but instead a few years apart (it's not specified how many). The brothers happen to look exactly like their father so that's why Alex thought it was her father. Through this interaction the Fairy-godmother decides to make a potion that will allow Lloyd to travel into his favorite books. Upon presenting it to him her heart sinks when he says that he has no interest in the potion whatsoever. She decides that the best way to please her son is to go into the hall of dreams and find out what it is that Lloyd desires. She finds that her son wants to overthrow her, become the next god-mother and cause destruction and mayhem. This is all that happens in the first chapter. <br /><br />It was very interesting to read about their adventures traveling into different books! I especially liked how Red was nominated to become the Lost Boy's mother. It was really cute to read. Conner used his magic for the first time without Alex. Bree and Emmerich's point of views come in this book. Alex's thing with King Arthur was unexpected along with Mother Goose and Merlin. I can actually see both couples working out but it's really weird considering that I was hoping that Alex would get back with Rook. Maybe she will, we'll just have to wait and see. I was pretty surprised that Mother Goose chose to stay in Camelot with Merlin. But whatever the case is she seems really happy and she did mention that whenever the twins need her she would come. As a parting gift she gives Alex Lester. When I read about Robin Hood and Peter Pan I was pretty annoyed with them. Peter had this thing for imitating Conner and Robbin Hood had a pretty large ego and yelled rather than speaking. I'm not sure what they are like in the original stories but this is what they are like in this book. The audience also discovers the identity of The Masked Man's son. <br /><br />The villain's for this book were as usual well done. I personally found the witches to be more intimidating than The Masked Man. The villains from the stories didn't play that big of a role. I can't wait to read about Red kicking Morina's (Thank you Alana for correcting me!) ass. <br /><br />Overall I am very excited to read the last book. I can hardly wait!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14685245277339412210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1315828732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1315828732" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

  <span id="freeText5018045902735308194" style="display:none">I'm not sure if this one was a bit lacking compared to the first two, or it was just me, but <b>I found this one to be mostly filler.</b><br /><br />There was around 100 pages of set up alone. I wasn't necessarily interested in that; I wanted to see Neverland and Oz!<br /><br />I know I've said this before, but <b>it really bothers me that every single word with even slight significance to what's happening is italicized.</b> I just feel like that could be toned down quite a bit.<br /><br />I mean, I still really like characters- especially Red! She's quite hilarious and I really enjoy every scene she's in.<br /><br />I really enjoyed book three, but <b>I didn't feel like much happened in this one.</b> As far as advancements in plot, twists and turns, it felt very lackluster.<br /><br />I really hope I'm not outgrowing books like these, since I do enjoy reading middle grade once in a while. <b>I hope the next one steps it up a bit, and I bet it will, being that we're preparing for battle by the end!</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1389265468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1389265468" />
    <a title="Devon Flaherty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17163060-devon-flaherty"><img alt="Devon Flaherty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442875304p2/17163060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1389265468?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Devon Flaherty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Devon Flaherty" href="/user/show/17163060-devon-flaherty">Devon Flaherty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Devon by: </span>
      my daughter
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1389265468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11617111277563260943">The Land of Stories series, by Chris Colfer, published from 2012-2015 by Little Brown. The series consists of four books so far, and Colfer says the series will end with the fifth book, assumed to be published in 2016. I read the series because my daughter–and just about every other kid her age–is in to the series, and there was no way she was waiting until next year to read the first four.<br/><br/>The series is:<br/><br/> The Wishing Spell<br/> The Enchantress Returns<br/> A Grimm Warning<br/> Beyond the Kingdoms<br/> An un-announce</span>
  <span id="freeText11617111277563260943" style="display:none">The Land of Stories series, by Chris Colfer, published from 2012-2015 by Little Brown. The series consists of four books so far, and Colfer says the series will end with the fifth book, assumed to be published in 2016. I read the series because my daughter–and just about every other kid her age–is in to the series, and there was no way she was waiting until next year to read the first four.<br /><br />The series is:<br /><br /> The Wishing Spell<br /> The Enchantress Returns<br /> A Grimm Warning<br /> Beyond the Kingdoms<br /> An un-announced fifth book<br /> At least three spin-offs, coming out later this year<br /><br /><br />I really don’t like giving scathing reviews. But I don’t know if there is any other way for me to do this. I want to be all nice and give Chris Colfer a pat on his talented back, but for this, I can not. Absolutely. Can. Not.<br /><br />I’m not exactly sure what it is about this series: the idea, the cover art, the marketing… but you want to like it. In fact, even as you are reading it, you still want to like the story. But there are so many obstacles, so many many obstacles, which begin with predictable and been-done. I knew almost all of the outcomes from near the beginning. I love the GoodReads review from Brett Axel, that asks, “What if C.S. Lewis, instead of honing his writing skills, watched lots of Shrek and Hoodwinked movies?” We are already getting to the point where we’ve seen way too much fractured fairy tale, and this one takes the been-done cake.<br /><br />Which in itself would not be terrible. Doing something “old” well justifies itself if you do it well enough. But this one, not even close. Let’s just jump right in.<br /><br />CHRIS COLFERMy daughter mentions frequently that mostly girls are drawn to the series. It doesn’t take a rocket scientist to figure out that only girls are going to tolerate all the outfit descriptions. Every time we encounter a new character, action pauses and Colfer gives a straight-forward, bland description. Example: “The Snow Queen was a tall woman with a large white fur coat, a snowflake crown, and a cloth wrapped around her eyes. Her skin was so pale and frostbitten it was practically blue. She had a strong jaw and tiny jagged teeth.” (By the way, where are the serial commas in that?) Mostly what a reader gets from this book series are prompts to imagine the story along with the writer. Mostly girls are going to enjoy this type of visual, especially about skin tone, clothing, and hair, not to mention the castles, throne rooms, and thrones. Then couple all that with the terrible action scenes. No, really terrible, and boys just aren’t going to be quite as interested.<br /><br />But that’s just the tip of the iceberg, a random introduction to the issues with this series. Here’s a list of some of the many, many things that constantly distracted me from enjoying the books (and yes, I read every word of the available books):<br /><br /> Remedial writing. I just couldn’t get past it. I would swear Colfer wrote this as a teenager, or even a junior-higher.<br /> Distracting and over-used adverbs<br /> Slang. Modern, timely phraseology and expressions<br /> Dangling pronouns<br /> Inconsistencies<br /> Misused words, like “got ahold of” and “dived”<br /> Terrible action scenes (which don’t always make spatial sense)<br /> Abbreviated heightened-tension areas and drawn out other areas<br /> Confusion<br /> Swear words? (Colfer has intimated that this series is for the kid in us grown-ups, but it is clearly written for a middle grades audience)<br /> Geographical issues<br /> Hyperbole! Lots of “always,” “never,” mixed with “almost never,” and “nearly always,” etc.<br /> Telling, not showing: like the worst I’ve seen<br /> Passive verbs<br /> Passive language<br /> Coincidences! not obstacles<br /> Mixed prepositions<br /> Complete lack of flow (writing intuition)<br /> Jarring perspective shifts<br /> Unrealistic reactions<br /> Timing issues (especially while characters are conversing)<br /> Hackneyed conversation<br /> A blatant lack of editing, including obvious spelling and grammar mistakes. Chandler is printed as “chandelier”?!?<br /><br />If you name a writing rule, it was broken ten ways.<br /><br />I have to mention it again–and I also want to point out that I have company in this opinion–that I really felt like I was reading the work of a very determined teenager. And while I applaud the effort, I would rather see the content in someone’s more capable hands. Or not at all… I mean, this story has been told before, and it wasn’t nearly as cheesy the first time around.<br /><br />What I really wonder–and was even distracted by the thought as I read–was if Colfer should have written this series as a screenplay, instead. Especially when you read sentences like this: “Reruns of a dramatic television show set in outer space did nothing to stop his procrastination.” Or, “The Enchantress forced out a theatrical laugh that did little to comfort him.” Dramatic television show? Theatrical laugh? This would be great for staging direction.<br /><br />And the thought is furthered by all the telling, instead of showing. Like this: “The Evil Queen looked down at him coldly. She had no sympathy left inside her for anyone.”<br /><br />By the time I got to the second book, I was hoping the writing had drastically improved with the series’ popularity. Even the first couple paragraphs have you going. But then right there, near the beginning, I was sad to be submitted to a terrible (and slightly insulting), in-no-way-covert attempt at arguing with his critics. Colfer highjacks a character to argue for him that writing does not need to be “high” writing, as long as it has passion. But let’s be honest. Simple writing includes the likes of Ernest Hemingway and William Carlos William’s wheelbarrow poem. The distinction between “simple” writing and “high” writing is not one between “good” and “bad,” or even between “passion” and “dispassion,” so Colfer is arguing oranges and apples, and doing it in the wrong place, besides. Passion may be a boon, but it does not make up for other things, like hard work, practice, education, natural talent, quality, etc. It’s like Colfer’s arguing for the participation award. Let’s compare these “simple” sentences:<br /><br />“so much depends / upon // a red wheel / barrow // glazed with rain / water // beside the white / chickens.” -William Carlos Williams, “The Red Wheelbarrow”<br /><br />“‘They’ll keep out of my way,’ she insisted. ‘It takes two to make an accident’” -F. Scott Fitzgerald, The Great Gatsby<br /><br />“‘Fish,” he said softly, aloud, ‘I’ll stay with you until I’m dead.'” -Ernest Hemingway, The Old Man and the Sea<br /><br />“Aunty had a way of declaring What Is Best For The Family, and I suppose her coming to live with us was in that category.” -Harper Lee, To Kill a Mockingbird<br /><br />And I’ll have you know, as beautiful as all this writing is, Colfer has better ratings just about anywhere. Oh. My. Goodness.<br /><br />I was so frustrated at one point, reading the book, that I stopped on the sentence I was at and asked, how would I re-write this? The sentence then went from “What had once been an imposing structure was just a massive pile of stone bricks and pieces of wood now,” to: What was once a majestic fortress had been reduced to a mountain of broken stone and splintered wood. Do you need me to walk you through the problems with the first sentence? It’s weak, imprecise, choppy, anachronistic (dimension-speaking), and distracting. I could do this to any sentence in the whole series, except for (maybe) the first paragraph of the third book, which Colfer seems to have polished up especially well… that is, until a carriage is shooting “like a cannonball” through a dense forest with a narrow, curvy path.<br /><br />The real battle here is NOT whether or not Colfer’s style is simple, but whether it’s bad or worse and whether or not that means we should avoid reading it and discourage our children as well. Should we swallow a very popular book and all its bad art with its vaguely intriguing story and color-matching faeries in order to have some entertainment? One of the things that can really drive a person crazy in the arts biz is just this quandary. Because, while people swallow bad art in the name of being entertained (or titillated) every day, there are so many artists out there willing and trying to provide a product that is both beautiful and entertaining. In this sense, it matters more who holds the keys to the kingdom and not who’s making royalty-worthy art.<br /><br />And why aspire to great, or even good art, anyhow? What if no one wants it? Is the aesthetic a value unto itself? Is it a question of truth? Or reality? Or physicality: symmetry and alliteration? Or a Platonic form or God-ward longing? Are truth and beauty their own rewards? And am I in the position to encourage others to find the gems among the rough and discourage the fool’s gold?<br /><br />Yes, I suppose that is exactly why I write reviews. After all, I don’t get paid for telling you if a book series stinks or if a novel deserves a standing ovation. And not that I am always correct in my reading. But while on one hand I want to be gentle and kind, I also feel excited to exalt the worthy or to push the mediocre to rise to the occasion.<br /><br />So in the end, I find this extremely popular series to be terrible to a fault. My daughter reads it. No, she loves it. She is ten, and she anxiously awaits the next book, which I will buy for her. I would not say that reading bad literature is exactly harmless fun, but I will point out that I survived far worse than Land of Stories, and I expect my daughter to–through a life of reading and conversations with myself and others–eventually see the series for what it really is. She’ll probably fall in line with the rest of us, War and Peace under one arm and a battered old copy of The Wishing Spell under the other.<br /><br />***REVIEW WRITTEN FOR THE DEVON TREVARROW FLAHERTY/STARVING ARTIST BLOG***</span>
  <a data-text-id="11617111277563260943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1327465349?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thibaut Nicodème" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thibaut Nicodème" href="/user/show/22674620-thibaut-nicod-me">Thibaut Nicodème</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1327465349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6822065927928854536">Well. That took a surprisingly dark turn.<br/><br/>But…you know, this book is <i>great</i>. Also, I love that it's basically tying together elements from the entire series and building up. Yay for no more fetch quest! (Well, there's still one, because tradition, but it only takes a couple chapters)<br/><br/>There's just so much for the next book to pay off on, though. That's one huge escalation compared to the previous, mostly self-contained books. And <i>I love it so much</i>.<br/><br/>Aside from that, it bears repeating that Chris Colfe</span>
  <span id="freeText6822065927928854536" style="display:none">Well. That took a surprisingly dark turn.<br /><br />But…you know, this book is <i>great</i>. Also, I love that it's basically tying together elements from the entire series and building up. Yay for no more fetch quest! (Well, there's still one, because tradition, but it only takes a couple chapters)<br /><br />There's just so much for the next book to pay off on, though. That's one huge escalation compared to the previous, mostly self-contained books. And <i>I love it so much</i>.<br /><br />Aside from that, it bears repeating that Chris Colfer's writing and humor speak to me, so I really have no complaints there. Though I am curious just how much this book is really still a children's book, and not in a "it's good and I like it as an adult so it can't be a child's book" way (I love plenty of children's stuff, and they're children's stuff) but more in a "can children really appreciate this sort of jokes/deviation from the original?" kind of way. Oh well.<br /><br />I have but one complaint to make, and it's this: did Alex really need another love interest? And another doomed one at that? (Though I guess he could always come back. There would be room—and justification—for it.)<br /><br /><br />Anyway, this book is great, this series is great, go read it.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1418018909" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1418018909" />
    <a title="Corey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47981640-corey"><img alt="Corey" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1418018909?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corey" href="/user/show/47981640-corey">Corey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1418018909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9957468107525345798">The Land of Stories: Beyond The Kingdoms is the fourth book in The Land of Stories series. It is about twins, Alex and Conner Bailey. In this book Alex and Conner are looking for the Masked Man, who Alex thinks is their deceased father. They are looking for him because he possesses a magical and powerful potion that turns any book it touches into a portal that leads into that certain book. The overall goal of the Masked Man is to gather an army of literature’s worst villains so that he can overt</span>
  <span id="freeText9957468107525345798" style="display:none">The Land of Stories: Beyond The Kingdoms is the fourth book in The Land of Stories series. It is about twins, Alex and Conner Bailey. In this book Alex and Conner are looking for the Masked Man, who Alex thinks is their deceased father. They are looking for him because he possesses a magical and powerful potion that turns any book it touches into a portal that leads into that certain book. The overall goal of the Masked Man is to gather an army of literature’s worst villains so that he can overthrow the Land of Stories. Because of this, Alex and Conner gather a group of friends to help look for him. With this group of friends, Alex and Conner follow the Masked Man through the Land of Oz, Neverland, Camelot, etc. Will they catch up with the Masked Man? Or will they be too late?<br /> I personally, really liked this book. I liked this book because of the plot. I liked the plot because it was easy to follow. For example, each chapter is about a different subject, making it easy to know what is going on at all times. I also liked this book because of the characters. I liked the characters because they were people/creatures from storybooks. For example, some of the characters were Mother Goose, Jack (from “Jack and The Beanstalk”), Goldilocks, Red Riding Hood and many others.<br /> To me, this writing is powerful. It is powerful because in the book there is a set of boy and girl twins named Alex and Conner, and I am a twin with a girl, just like Conner. Also Alex’s names starts with an A and my twins name Abby, starts with an A and Conner’s name starts with a C and my name Corey, starts with a C. I would recommend this book to anyone that likes adventure, action, or fantasy. I will continue to read The Land of Stories series, when the next book comes out. Overall, I think The Land of Stories: Beyond The Kingdoms is a great book, with an amazing storyline, that anyone should read if they are interested in adventure, action, or fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9957468107525345798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2794321881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2794321881" />
    <a title="explorerofbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34290393-explorerofbooks"><img alt="explorerofbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559223817p2/34290393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2794321881?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="explorerofbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="explorerofbooks" href="/user/show/34290393-explorerofbooks">explorerofbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2794321881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2253896982618284134"><i>The Land of Stories</i> series is a set of middle grade books that know fully well how to capture adult readers, mostly by its humor. It is a wild collision of fantasy, fairytales, mystery and adventure. An excellent experience for fans of <i>Narnia</i> and <i>Once Upon A Time</i>, or young adults who understand how long stories from our early days can linger in our mind. Luckily, the fourth book did not disappoint. <br/><br/>With the Masked Man on the loose, it’s up to the Bailey twins to stop him. Only problem? He might </span>
  <span id="freeText2253896982618284134" style="display:none"><i>The Land of Stories</i> series is a set of middle grade books that know fully well how to capture adult readers, mostly by its humor. It is a wild collision of fantasy, fairytales, mystery and adventure. An excellent experience for fans of <i>Narnia</i> and <i>Once Upon A Time</i>, or young adults who understand how long stories from our early days can linger in our mind. Luckily, the fourth book did not disappoint. <br /><br />With the Masked Man on the loose, it’s up to the Bailey twins to stop him. Only problem? He might be part of their family, and on top of that, the Fairy Council doesn’t see the danger. Together with their loyal friends, Connor and Alex discover the Masked Man can turn books into portals. Their world goes farther than fairytales when they have to wade through Neverland, Camelot and other peculiar realms to refrain the Masked Man from bringing back every notorious villain ever read about.<br /><br />Chris Colfer once again proved how imaginative his take on our childhood tales is. We go further than the Land of Stories in this sequel. The setting abruptly changes after 100 pages or so, leading us to other worlds of literature. We also frequently return to the Otherworld, where Emmerich and Bree discover important facts about their heritage. Colfer finally explores his creative realm by introducing characters that influenced the past, hereby tying all elements from the series neatly together. The involved classic literature included many of my favorites: <i>The Wizard of Oz, Peter Pan, Alice In Wonderland, King Arthur, Robin Hood</i>, and even Greek mythology. It made me relive the tales from another perspective, which turned out to be a compelling adventure. The book solved some questions the previous novels had raised, which confirms to me that this young writer knows exactly what he’s doing. The new twists just kept appearing without warning, building up to a quick, spine-tingling pacing.<br /><br />It’s intriguing to see how all our favorite characters are maturing. Goldilocks and Jacks are still as brave and strong-minded as before, even though they are expecting a newcomer into their happy family. Red is becoming less self-absorbed after realizing what she truly wants in life, and Connor still has some more confidence to grow. Maybe the most fascinating development, especially considering the young target group, is meant for Alex. Run over by her emotions, it’s impossible for her to control her powers. The moments she can’t hold back anymore are highly entertaining, seeing that she has some unique powers. Not only can she make crowded buildings fly, she can also squeeze veins tight enough to nearly choke her enemies. Our hero might be turning into a villain, which learns kids something about personal motivation and perception.<br /><br />Our main villain hasn’t changed from the last book, but we do get more background information now. Readers might feel sympathy for the Masked Man now we learn he was mistreated. Another thought-provoking dynamic is his familial relationship to the heroes. Granted, I would have loved to see bigger roles for the classic villains already, but they always immediately disappeared. Yet, it seems like <i>Beyond The Kingdoms</i> remarkably influenced the arising war, so that leaves more to be seen in the sequel.<br /><br /><b>Even though exceedingly entertaining, the novel mostly had a filler plot. Conflict or action was barely mentioned. It still demands for 4 stars, because of the educational value these books have. While it was unnecessary and offsetting to explain the main plot twist in the first chapter, <i>Beyond The Kingdoms</i> defines the importance of self-discovery and going against expectations. It also describes how racism starts, adding some emotional weight. One of Colfer’s strengths is definitely his humor. Here we have Mother Goose occasionally referring to the Otherworld, and so confusing all fairytale characters. The Merlin shown here also reminded me more of the Shrek version, which I’ve always found hilarious. With its whimsical storytelling, <i> The Land of Stories</i> is a series not to be missing out on. </b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2253896982618284134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1137494592" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1137494592" />
    <a title="ella " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37003394-ella"><img alt="ella " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475186518p2/37003394.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1137494592?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ella " class="user" itemprop="url" name="ella " href="/user/show/37003394-ella">ella </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316348034" href="/book/show/25870977-beyond-the-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37003394-ella?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37003394-ella?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37003394-ella?shelf=should-be-a-movie">should-be-a-movie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37003394-ella?shelf=caution-contains-cliffhanger">caution-contains-cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37003394-ella?shelf=could-not-put-down">could-not-put-down</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1137494592&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1137494592" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15416162010619653055">There were a few flaws, but overall, Beyond the Kingdoms will be rated five stars. It's one of my new favourites, and it keeps you wanting to keep turning the pages.<br/><br/>In the fourth book in the Land of Stories series, Alex and Conner are about fifteen years old. The timing takes place about five months after the events in a Grimm Warning, the third book. In this book, we travel from Oz and meet the "heartless" Tin Woodman, to Wonderland, but I don't think we meet anyone there, to Neverland, where w</span>
  <span id="freeText15416162010619653055" style="display:none">There were a few flaws, but overall, Beyond the Kingdoms will be rated five stars. It's one of my new favourites, and it keeps you wanting to keep turning the pages.<br><br>In the fourth book in the Land of Stories series, Alex and Conner are about fifteen years old. The timing takes place about five months after the events in a Grimm Warning, the third book. In this book, we travel from Oz and meet the "heartless" Tin Woodman, to Wonderland, but I don't think we meet anyone there, to Neverland, where we meet Peter and the Lost Boys, to the world of King Arthur, where we meet Merlin and Arthur and Robin Hood, where we meet Robin Hood and the Merry Men. This book contains a cliffhanger, just not as extreme as the third book. <br><br>Here are some good things about the book. Firstly, the <b>adventure</b>. I loved hearing about all the places, although the time in Wonderland was shorter. My favourite was probably Oz, or Neverland, or King Arthur... I can't choose, I loved them all! Then, the <b>drama.</b> I was practically dead during Red and Froggy's wedding when You-Know-Who showed up. Not Voldemort, another You-Know-Who. And then what the woman did to Froggy... oh my god! It wasn't nesscessarily drama, but there was a lot of 'dramatic' romance between Arthur and Alex. Especially the way they described Alex walking away from him. It was like a soap opera. Also, the <b>ending</b>. I really wished that there was more, this book being the least amount of pages, but it's still a really exciting ending. I can't wait to see Conner's book characters. One last thing about all the other things I could share that would make this an even longer review was the <b>visualisation</b>. Getting into the books, the way it was described looked so awesome. If I had the capability of using the Portal Potion, I'd have a million books to go into and characters to meet. <br><br>And now for a few flaws. It was annoying to read <b>Robin Hood's speech</b>. His speech was always in cap locks, which made it kind of annoying to read. Apparently he shouts when he speaks, but still, I didn't find the cap locks very neescessary. Another thing was the <b>italics</b>. Oh my gosh, there was so much italics in places that it didn't need. It will make it seem like the characters were emphasizing everything they said. <br>"Most ancient civilizations were influenced by creatures that are considered <i>mythical</i> today. The ancient people paid tribute to these beings in their art, stories, and sometimes even worshipped them. Despite the obvious presence of these creatures, historians have labeled their existence as <i>mythology</i> - simply because they don't meet the biological standards of animals today."<br>"Ancient Asia was majorly influenced by <i>dragons</i>, Europe is crawling with legends of <i>fairies</i> and <i>trolls</i> living in its forests, the Vikings claimed to witness <i>merpeople</i> as they sailed across the oceans and that's only naming a few."<br>I know that might not be that bad, but if you read the whole book, you'll realize this is overused.<br><br>Other than those couple of things, Beyond the Kingdoms is rated 5 stars. It's one of my favourite books, and obsessions. I highly recommend it. Once I finish the last book next year, I'm going to die. This book, this series, really should be a movie. It's so awesome, awesome, and did I say awesome, and would be a really awesome movie if it's made well. I love the series!!!!!! <br><br>Also, feel free to join the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148041" rel="nofollow noopener">Land of Stories group</a> if you're a fan! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423429620ra/13624204.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15416162010619653055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1468846333" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1468846333" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21548465-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533175941p2/21548465.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1468846333?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/21548465-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21548465-kristen?shelf=audiobook-reads">audiobook-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1468846333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14461577557458623110">I've really liked this series throughout, but this installment was a big disappointment. First of all, this one tries to incorporate EVERY SINGLE CHARACTER we have seen so far in the series--sometimes dedicating whole chapters to characters who play no role in the story at all. (Like Bree and Emmerich--I'm assuming the only reason they were even in this one is either because Colfer felt bad leaving them behind or to set up the next book.) On top of that, we have MORE NEW CHARACTERS to worry abou</span>
  <span id="freeText14461577557458623110" style="display:none">I've really liked this series throughout, but this installment was a big disappointment. First of all, this one tries to incorporate EVERY SINGLE CHARACTER we have seen so far in the series--sometimes dedicating whole chapters to characters who play no role in the story at all. (Like Bree and Emmerich--I'm assuming the only reason they were even in this one is either because Colfer felt bad leaving them behind or to set up the next book.) On top of that, we have MORE NEW CHARACTERS to worry about and keep track of. It's just too much and doesn't allow the story to focus on...well...anything. <br /><br />Which brings me to the next problem: there is no story here. No build up of tension, no climax. The problem is presented almost immediately: the masked man is recruiting an army of villains from literature (Captain Hook, the Wicked Witch, etc.). That problem is never solved--and the book is over 400 pages long! Not to mention the other problems that pop up along the way--AND ARE ALSO NEVER SOLVED. I hate books in a series that appear to exist only as a way to build up for a big bang in the next (or last) book--and this is one of the worst offenders I've read. Huge let down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14461577557458623110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cQUYLHlZP8k3fVidN9e9iZ/6tsr/+0t3fqx3J7NmcBI7dTy4v5e5+vdiMxGITmjQEfuC6d8vcS9qr2Xc4eHqHw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eOgq9IOpQ+mR0u1eP2i4wqbD1hGk2gsY+iF9ShXjCqEymA5gRWfF2lHNhtKA8W2bKMLiMoQOMUDuIm+xR2SQrA==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer6507505519352874548">Chris Colfer is an Emmy-nominated and Golden Globe-winning actor best-known for his portrayal of Kurt Hummel on the FOX television series "Glee". <br/><br/>He is also a New York Times bestselling author whose books include the first three novels in the "Land of Stories" series ("The Wishing Spell", "The Enchantress Returns" and "A Grimm Warning") as well as "Struck By Lightning: The Carson Philips Journal" </span>
  <span id="freeText6507505519352874548" style="display:none">Chris Colfer is an Emmy-nominated and Golden Globe-winning actor best-known for his portrayal of Kurt Hummel on the FOX television series "Glee". <br /><br />He is also a New York Times bestselling author whose books include the first three novels in the "Land of Stories" series ("The Wishing Spell", "The Enchantress Returns" and "A Grimm Warning") as well as "Struck By Lightning: The Carson Philips Journal" which is a novelization based on the script he wrote for the film "Struck By Lighting" (Colfer also co-produced and starred in that movie).</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/26526615-beyond-the-kingdoms-the-land-of-stories-4">Quotes from Beyond the Kingdoms</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Maybe greatness isn't about being immortal, or glorious, or popular - it's about choosing to fight for the greater good of the world, even when the world's turned its back on you.&rdquo;</span>
